r1818 | nbailey | 2019-06-24 11:59:59 +0200 (Mon, 24 Jun 2019) | 4 lines

Finished refactoring of molecule stuff. The user interface for adding molecular potentials is now essentially the same as that for non-molecular ones: create the object, call SetParams, add it to the Simulation object using AddPotential which now handles both non-molecular and molecular potentials. Also, SetPotential is deprecated. Some other details are changed: For bond potentials the bond length argument is called simply length, and for harmonic and FENE the stiffness argument is called stiffness. For harmonic and FENE bonds the user has to explicitly choose whether to exlude a given bond type (no default). For Constraints exclusion is enforced always. For angle and dihedral potentials one chooses exclude (defauolt is true) for all angle- or dihedral- types together. GetAngles and GetDihedrals have been removed from Simulation--one can get them from molecule data (sim.GetMoleculeData().GetAngles()).
Molecular potentials are stored on a separate data structure in Simulation to ensure only one object of each type is present.Tests and documentation have been changed to reflect the altered interface. A lot of code to do with setting molecular potentials has been removed. ResetNeighborList for PairPotentials has been replaced by a general potential function called ResetInternalData (to allow eg ConstraintPotential to rebuild its data structures during autotuning, without the autotuner needing to know about ConstraintPotential). Molecular potentials now have a SetExclusions function which calls the appropriate function in MoleculeData (bond/angle/dihedral), saving a lot of code in Simulation. Some general tidying also done: removing old commented-out code, fixing comments and docstrings, etc.

r1811 | nbailey | 2019-05-28 15:35:33 +0200 (Tue, 28 May 2019) | 2 lines

Second phase of refactoring MoleculeData. Not complete yet --- the end goal is to have the user create the molecular potential objects the same way they create the atomic potential objects. The management of these objects will be moved into Simulation but so far this has been only done for bond potentials (harmonic/FENE/constraint). The user accesses these via Simulation methods for now (previously via MoleculeData). A general SetBondData method has been added to MoleculeData so the latter doesn't need to know about the various different types of bond potentials. Small fixes to Sample.GetStresses() function and to RUMD_Test.

r1789 | nbailey | 2018-12-17 16:35:02 +0100 (Mon, 17 Dec 2018) | 2 lines

First of a series of changes intended to reduce the complexity of the object structure of RUMD (as evidenced by doxygen for example), by removing unnecessary stored pointers. Here the focus was on bond, angle and dihedral potentials, which now no longer store a pointer to MoleculeData-instead they get via the sample pointer. This reduced interdependency and compile time, and will allow more interesting and flexible simulation processes through dynamic managing of objects.

------------------------------------------------------------------------

SetPositions should now work with sorting turned on. Changes made in rev 1769 have been removed as unnecessary.

r1741 | nbailey | 2017-11-26 14:20:11 +0100 (Sun, 26 Nov 2017) | 3 lines

Have made rumd "double-ready" with respect to use of atomicAdd, by including inline functions atomicFloatAdd and atomicDoubleAdd in rumd_algorithms.h. The former simply calls atomicAdd and is called everywhere in the code there was atomicAdd before. The latter is a software implementation, and will be called after doing search and replace to make a double-precision version of rumd.

r1537 | nbailey | 2015-01-28 22:34:06 +0100 (Wed, 28 Jan 2015) | 3 lines

In last commit added cudaDeviceSynchronize to Sample::CalcF before cudaGetLastError because the latter is not enough by itself to isolate device problems. But this checking, particular when cudaDeviceSynchronize is included, takes time, so now it is controlled by a variable which is by default false (no checking) but is true when the autotuner is running (because it is necessary to determine when tp is too large). It can also be turned on by the user if problems occur (sim.sample.SetCheckCudaErrors(True)).

------------------------------------------------------------------------
r1097 | nbailey | 2012-03-27 12:44:10 +0200 (Tue, 27 Mar 2012) | 4 lines

Added RUMD_cudaResourceError, derived from RUMD_Error to allow smooth handling
of resource errors by the autotuner arising from setting tp too high. This generates a ValueError at the Python level (as opposed to a RuntimeError). Added functions to generate combined error strings (cuts down on SWIG-generated  wrapper code). Changed the class name from Autotuner to Autotune (to match the module name).  Removed code which tries to figure out which tp values are safe. All are tried and those which raise exceptions are then avoided. Fixed a bug in ParticleData::AllocateParticles() involving not copying the host data data when re-allocating due to change of pb. This particularly affected types in saved configurations.


------------------------------------------------------------------------
r1096 | heine | 2012-03-26 19:42:28 +0200 (Mon, 26 Mar 2012) | 1 line

remove hardcoded -m64 option to allow compiling on i386
------------------------------------------------------------------------
r1095 | nbailey | 2012-03-22 16:09:59 +0100 (Thu, 22 Mar 2012) | 2 lines

Made Autotune safer by making a more conservative estimate of the number of registers per thread (66, which seems to be the maximum over all instantiations of md_calc_f). The user can change this simply by at.reg_per_thread=X (where at is the Autotuner object) before calling the Tune function.

r1084 | nbailey | 2012-03-02 14:31:31 +0100 (Fri, 02 Mar 2012) | 2 lines

Have all but completed ioformat2. A variable rumd_ioformat in rumd_base.h controls the default format for both energies and configurations. The format for the latter can be turned on using Sample::SetConfIO_Format. All tests pass when ioformat=2 is used and restarting SLLOD also works. Have managed to simplify the way the comment line is read so both formats can be read, and everything works, without the user needing to do anything. The mechanism involves functions GetInoString SimulationBox and Integrator classes, functions SetBoxParameters(replacing SetBoxDetails) in SimulationBox classes, and functions InitializeFromInfoString in Integrator classes. There is also a global function ParseFromInfoString.

r941 | trond | 2011-05-04 13:33:51 +0200 (Wed, 04 May 2011) | 1 line

It is now possible to thermostat specific types of particles with itg.SetThermostatOnParticleType(type=0, on=0/1). IntegratorNVT needs to adjust the DOFs read from Sample to take into account the true thermostat.

r905 | nbailey | 2011-03-16 10:48:28 +0100 (Wed, 16 Mar 2011) | 2 lines

Added a vector to contain the potentials in IHS_OutputManager, since it creates the copies and is therefore responsible for destroying them. Added remaining Copy functions to PairPotentials and introduced an object index for PairPotential objects to be used to allow different objects to have their own block of constant memory for parameters. At the moment it comes from a static counter that increments each time a PairPotential object is created.

r904 | nbailey | 2011-03-14 15:54:11 +0100 (Mon, 14 Mar 2011) | 2 lines

Changed InherentStateCalculator to IHS_OutputManager, ie from an ExternalCalculator (which puts things into the main energies file) to	 a separate OutputManager. This was necessary to be able to also save minimized configurations. The ihs energies are also now in a separate file (which includes virial, maximum force, and number of iterations taken). Added a Copy function to potentials, by which they can generate a copy of themselves (for use by the IHS_OutputManager for example). Only implemented for Pot_LJ_12_6 so far. Small changes to RUMD_Test and a couple other places.

r884 | tbs | 2010-12-13 10:00:30 +0100 (Mon, 13 Dec 2010) | 2 lines

Added option 'm' (particles per molecule). If this is greater than zero msd and Fs will also be calculated for center of masses, assuming that all molecules have 'm' particles, and that they these are stored in order (i.e., molecule 0 consists of particles 0 to m-1 etc). Eventually, topology information stored in mol.top should be used.

r675 | nbailey | 2010-08-11 21:45:02 +0200 (Wed, 11 Aug 2010) | 2 lines

Have made an interface to Python which can reproduce the functionality of a typical user program. An example script, which emulates rumd_LJ, is to be found in the Python directory. To compile the Python extension, do "make swig". Then you need to add the rumd directory to your PYTHONPATH environment variable. To make the interface work I needed to make a class to contain md_device_init. I also needed to add some conditional compilation  in integrator headers to hide kernel delcarations from swig.

r617 | nbailey | 2010-07-14 14:09:16 +0200 (Wed, 14 Jul 2010) | 2 lines

Replaced the code for LogLin output with similar code in external classes. Old code is still present but commented out. It will be cleaned up later. There is no change in behavior, except (1) restart file number XXXX now contains the configuration at the beginning of block XXXX not the one at the end. (2) The user must call SetIOBlockInfo (this was optional before, and may become so again, by setting up a default system) and this must be before the energyWriteInterval is set (by a new function SetEnergyWriteInterval). This may also change. (3) A previously unnoticed (by me at least) bug regarding the timeStepIndex in trajectory files was fixed (this is unrelated to the other changes). Reference files for tests have been updated.

I felt this should be separate in order for people to be more easilty able to add functions corresponding to new potentials.

r288 | heine | 2009-11-22 21:51:38 +0100 (Sun, 22 Nov 2009) | 7 lines

add a file (.svnignore) with filenames to let subversion ignore.
Changes to the file has to be followed up by the command:
svn proset svn:ignore --file .svnignore .
Both changes (changes to .svnignore and to the directory property list) has to be committed.
The svn:ignore property on current directory can be listed with the comman
svn propget svn:ignore .

r119 | nbailey | 2009-07-02 14:32:34 +0200 (Thu, 02 Jul 2009) | 2 lines

Added a test program which makes it easy to check whether code changes affect simulation output. The program is in  ConsistencyTest001.cu and the associated input files and script are Test/SimpleConsistencyTests. Running the script test.pbs (in mode 2, the default) in that directory will run simulations in the separate subdirectories and concatenate the results of comparing against existing output files  into a file status.txt. If the string FAIL appears in the latter there is a problem. If there is a good reason for it then the test script should be run again in mode 1 to create new versions of the output files.
